# 2025 r/Fantasy Bingo Stats

This page contains summary statistics for the whole card. Individual square statistics can be found at the following links:

|---|---|---|---|---|
|[Knights and Paladins](knights-and-paladins)|[Hidden Gem](hidden-gem)|[Published in the 80s](published-in-the-80s)|[High Fashion](high-fashion)|[Down With the System](down-with-the-system)|
|[Impossible Places](impossible-places)|[A Book in Parts](a-book-in-parts)|[Gods and Pantheons](gods-and-pantheons)|[Last in a Series](last-in-a-series)|[Book Club or Readalong Book](book-club-or-readalong-book)|

## Square and Card Statistics

- There were 1548 cards submitted, 694 of which were incomplete.
The minimum number of filled squares was 5. 536 were *this close*, with 24 filled squares.
1768 squares were left blank, leaving 36932 filled squares.
- There were 37756 total stories, with 13193 unique stories read,
by 7658 unique authors (38165 total).
9787 books and 5016 authors were used only once. 
- The top squares left blank were: **Not a Book**, blank on 604 cards; **Published in the 80s**, blank on 79 cards; **Five Short Stories**, blank on 75 cards. On the other hand, **LGBTQIA Protagonist** was only left blank 26 times.
- The squares most often substituted were: **Published in the 80s**, substituted on 61 cards; **Hidden Gem** and **Pirates**, substituted on 46 cards each; **Five Short Stories**, substituted on 43 cards.
**Down With the System** and **Recycle a Bingo Square** were never substituted.
This means that Not a Book was the least favorite overall, skipped or substituted a total of 644 times, and
Recycle a Bingo Square was the favorite, skipped or substituted only 28 times.
- There were an average of 6.3 unique books per card.
- 126 cards claimed an all-hard-mode card, while 70 cards were short by one square.
89 cards claimed no hard-mode squares at all. The average number of hard-mode squares per card was 11.9.
There were a total of 18381 hard-mode squares claimed.

One of those interesting stats phenomena: even though most cards only include a few unique books, most of the books read are unique.
There were an average of 2.8 reads per book.

As with books, most authors were read only once.
There were an average of 5.0 reads per author.

The following tables represent a best-effort attempt at a statistical breakdown of author demographics.
The "Overall %" column represents the _total_ number of times a demographic appeared in Bingo data,
i.e. Brandon Sanderson counts 394 times for each of his demographic groups.
The "Unique %" column represents the unique number of times a demographic appeared in Bingo data,
i.e. Brandon Sanderson counts only once, no matter how many squares or cards he appears on.

Demographics representing less than 1% of the unique authors are not included in these tables.

## Bingo-type Statistics

### Normal Mode

There were 16083 complete bingos.
Non-blackout cards completed an average of 8.4 bingos.
There were 18 cards that did not complete any bingos.

The hardest bingo by number of cards was Fourth Row, incomplete on 674 cards.
The hardest bingo by number of squares was Fourth Row, with a total of 856 squares left blank.

The easiest bingo by number of cards was Second Column, incomplete on 95 cards.
The easiest bingo by number of squares was First Row, with a total of 178 squares left blank.

## Book Variety (Per Square)

The FarraGini index, [introduced in 2017](https://www.reddit.com/r/Fantasy/comments/89esvx/2017_fantasy_bingo_statistics/) (see Part III),
attempts to measure the variety of books and authors read for each square.
Each entity's "income" for a square is the number of times it was used for that square,
so the index is analogous to its namesake, the [Gini index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gini_coefficient):

Values close to 0 suggest a square was well-varied; 0 means no book was repeated for a square.
Values close to 100 suggest the same books were used repeatedly for a square; 100 means only one book was used for a square.

|SQUARE #|SQUARE|BOOK|AUTHOR|
|:---------:|---------|:---------:|:---------:|
|1|Knights and Paladins|62.4|72.1|
|2|Hidden Gem|14.6|23.2|
|3|Published in the 80s|59.1|70.7|
|4|High Fashion|62.9|69.7|
|5|Down With the System|44.9|57.3|
|6|Impossible Places|52.5|62.9|
|7|A Book in Parts|40.9|55.2|
|8|Gods and Pantheons|42.7|59.3|
|9|Last in a Series|39.5|50.1|
|10|Book Club or Readalong Book|54.0|57.9|
|11|Parents|45.6|55.9|
|12|Epistolary|63.0|70.1|
|13|Published in 2025|48.4|52.1|
|14|Author of Color|45.2|59.4|
|15|Small Press or Self-Published|21.8|32.3|
|16|Biopunk|64.3|72.6|
|17|Elves and Dwarves|55.8|69.9|
|18|LGBTQIA Protagonist|41.6|54.0|
|19|Five Short Stories|34.8|44.2|
|20|Stranger in a Strange Land|43.9|55.7|
|21|Recycle a Bingo Square|20.6|36.3|
|22|Cozy SFF|51.4|63.0|
|23|Generic Title|50.7|58.7|
|24|Not a Book|20.5|30.3|
|25|Pirates|54.6|63.6|
{: .sortable}

The squares with the most variety in books:
- **Hidden Gem**
- **Not a Book**
- **Recycle a Bingo Square**

The squares with the most variety in authors:
- **Hidden Gem**
- **Not a Book**
- **Small Press or Self-Published**

The squares with the least variety in books:
- **Biopunk**
- **Epistolary**
- **High Fashion**

The squares with the least variety in authors:
- **Biopunk**
- **Knights and Paladins**
- **Published in the 80s**

## Wall of Shame

Quoting the [very first bingo stats post](https://www.reddit.com/r/Fantasy/comments/62sp9h/2016_fantasy_bingo_statistics/),

> You are all terrible spellers.

A "misspelling" for the purposes of these statistics is any book (title/author combination)
that does not match the version used as the canonical version during cleaning.
There were a total of 3561 misspellings.
(Note that this does not include short stories.)

The books with the most variation in title or author spellings were:

- **This is How You Lose the Time War** by Amal El-Mohtar, Max Gladstone, with 25 variations
- **Blood Over Bright Haven** by M.L. Wang, with 20 variations
- ***TIE***: **The Adventures of Amina al-Sirafi** by Shannon Chakraborty and **The Sword of Kaigen** by M.L. Wang, with 14 variations each
- ***TIE***: **Howl's Moving Castle** by Diana Wynne Jones and **Mother of Learning** by Domagoj Kurmaić, with 11 variations each
- **Emily Wilde's Encyclopaedia of Faeries** by Heather Fawcett, with 9 variations
- ***TIE***: **Paladin's Grace** by T. Kingfisher and **The Spear Cuts Through Water** by Simon Jimenez and **The Tainted Cup** by Robert Jackson Bennett, with 8 variations each
- ***TIE***: **A Psalm for the Wild-Built** by Becky Chambers and **A Wizard of Earthsea** by Ursula K. Le Guin and **Sorcery & Cecelia: or The Enchanted Chocolate Pot** by Patricia C. Wrede, Caroline Stevermer and **The Fifth Season** by N.K. Jemisin and **The House in the Cerulean Sea** by T.J. Klune and **The Will of the Many** by James Islington, with 7 variations each
- ***TIE***: **A Memory of Light** by Robert Jordan, Brandon Sanderson and **Babel** by R.F. Kuang and **Beware of Chicken** by CasualFarmer and **Guards! Guards!** by Terry Pratchett and **Legends & Lattes** by Travis Baldree and **Somewhere Beyond the Sea** by T.J. Klune and **The Hobbit** by J.R.R. Tolkien and **The Left Hand of Darkness** by Ursula K. Le Guin and **The Mask of Mirrors** by M.A. Carrick, with 6 variations each
- ***TIE***: **A Sorceress Comes to Call** by T. Kingfisher and **All Systems Red** by Martha Wells and **Gideon the Ninth** by Tamsyn Muir and **He Who Fights with Monsters** by Shirtaloon and **Jonathan Strange & Mr. Norrell** by Susanna Clarke and **Leviathan Wakes** by James S.A. Corey and **Never Whistle at Night** by Shane Hawk, Theodore C. Van Alst Jr. and **Piranesi** by Susanna Clarke and **Ring Shout** by P. Djèlí Clark and **The City & the City** by China Miéville and **The City of Brass** by Shannon Chakraborty and **The Daughters’ War** by Christopher Buehlman and **The Dispossessed** by Ursula K. Le Guin and **The Fellowship of the Ring** by J.R.R. Tolkien and **The Word for World Is Forest** by Ursula K. Le Guin and **To Be Taught, If Fortunate** by Becky Chambers and **To Shape a Dragon's Breath** by Moniquill Blackgoose, with 5 variations each
- ***TIE***: **A Master of Djinn** by P. Djèlí Clark and **Before the Coffee Gets Cold** by Toshikazu Kawaguchi and **DallerGut Dream Department Store** by Lee Mi-ye and **Dungeon Crawler Carl** by Matt Dinniman and **Gods of Jade and Shadow** by Silvia Moreno-Garcia and **Gods of the Wyrdwood** by R.J. Barker and **Good Omens** by Neil Gaiman, Terry Pratchett and **I’m Afraid You’ve Got Dragons** by Peter S. Beagle and **Mistborn** by Brandon Sanderson and **Nettle & Bone** by T. Kingfisher and **Orconomics** by J. Zachary Pike and **The Black God's Drums** by P. Djèlí Clark and **The Book That Wouldn't Burn** by Mark Lawrence and **The Color of Magic** by Terry Pratchett and **The Dead Cat Tail Assassins** by P. Djèlí Clark and **The Eye of the Bedlam Bride** by Matt Dinniman and **The Invisible Life of Addie LaRue** by V.E. Schwab and **The Liar's Knot** by M.A. Carrick and **The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet** by Becky Chambers and **The Phoenix Keeper** by S.A. MacLean and **The Three-Body Problem** by Cixin Liu and **There Is No Antimemetics Division** by qntm and **Vita Nostra** by Marina Dyachenko, Sergey Dyachenko and **Water Moon** by Samantha Sotto Yambao, with 4 variations each

What makes a book hard to "spell" correctly?

- Length
- Lots of articles or prepositions
- Non-ASCII characters (diacritics, etc.)
- Lots of authors
- Numbers
- Somewhat obviously, books that were published under multiple titles

Predictably, there's a lot of crossover between books with the most variations and the most-read books overall.

Is it true that "every year we typo further from God"? Proportionally, we collectively seem to be improving,
though absolute numbers are still increasing. There may not be enough data to draw strong conclusions yet, though.
